● Now add a helper to look up step+1 data from the aggregate, and call it when filling delayed/SL fields. Update

● Update(trade_map_plotter_v34_lite_action.py)
  ⎿  Added 62 lines, removed 1 line
      659              if trade[f"sl{sl}_step"] is None and unrealized <= -sl:
      660                  trade[f"sl{sl}_step"] = step
      661
      662 +    def _lookup_step(self, step_num):
      663 +        """Look up close and reading for a given step from aggregate + signals.
      664 +        Returns (close, reading) or (None, None)."""
      665 +        if self._cached_df is None:
      666 +            return None, None
      667 +        df = self._cached_df
      668 +        if 'step' not in df.columns:
      669 +            return None, None
      670 +        mask = df['step'] == step_num
      671 +        if not mask.any():
      672 +            return None, None
      673 +        idx = mask.idxmax()
      674 +        close = float(self._cached_close_values[idx])
      675 +        # Find reading from signals list
      676 +        reading = None
      677 +        for sig in self.signals:
      678 +            if sig['step'] == step_num:
      679 +                reading = sig.get('signal')
      680 +                break
      681 +        return close, reading
      682 +
      683 +    def _fill_delayed_fields(self, trade):
      684 +        """Fill d_entry, d_exit, d_pnl from step+1 lookups."""
      685 +        # Delayed entry: step+1 after entry
      686 +        d_entry_step = trade["entry_step"] + 1
      687 +        d_entry_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_entry_step)
      688 +        trade["d_entry_step"] = d_entry_step
      689 +        trade["d_entry_close"] = d_entry_close
      690 +
      691 +        # Delayed exit: step+1 after exit
      692 +        if trade["exit_step"] is not None:
      693 +            d_exit_step = trade["exit_step"] + 1
      694 +            d_exit_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_exit_step)
      695 +            trade["d_exit_step"] = d_exit_step
      696 +            trade["d_exit_close"] = d_exit_close
      697 +
      698 +            if d_entry_close is not None and d_exit_close is not None:
      699 +                if trade["side"] == "call":
      700 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_exit_close - d_entry_close, 4)
      701 +                else:
      702 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_entry_close - d_exit_close, 4)
      703 +
      704 +    def _fill_sl_exit_fields(self, trade):
      705 +        """Fill sl*_next_step, sl*_next_close, sl*_next_reading, sl*_exit_pnl."""
      706 +        for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      707 +            sl_step = trade.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      708 +            if sl_step is not None:
      709 +                next_step = int(sl_step) + 1
      710 +                next_close, next_reading = self._lookup_step(next_step)
      711 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_step"] = next_step
      712 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_close"] = next_close
      713 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_reading"] = next_reading
      714 +                if next_close is not None:
      715 +                    if trade["side"] == "call":
      716 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(next_close - trade["entry_close"], 4)
      717 +                    else:
      718 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(trade["entry_close"] - next_close, 4)

● Header now shows: Trades - X total (Y closed: W=Z L=Z) | PNL: +X.XXXX | dPNL: +X.XXXX

> waht the import the module is using for iamge top bottom recodtion ?

● scan.py's detect_signal() uses:

  - OpenCV (cv2) — cv2.cvtColor for grayscale, cv2.Canny for edge detection
  - scipy (scipy.signal.find_peaks) — finds peaks (tops) and valleys (bottoms) in the smoothed edge curve
  - scipy (scipy.ndimage.gaussian_filter1d) — smooths the edge y-values before peak finding

  The flow:
  1. cv2.Canny(gray, 50, 150) — finds edges in the WMA line image
  2. For each x column, average the y-coordinates of edge pixels
  3. gaussian_filter1d(y_vals, sigma=1) — smooth the curve
  4. find_peaks(y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds bottoms (valleys)
  5. find_peaks(-y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds tops (peaks)
  6. Rightmost bottom > rightmost top → call, otherwise → put

✻ Sautéed for 34s

> sofi is hi vol stock ?

● Yes, SOFI (SoFi Technologies) is a high volume stock. It typically trades 200-400M+ shares daily, making it one of the
   most actively traded stocks on NASDAQ. That's why the 720k/1440k volume bar thresholds work — with that much volume,
  bars fill quickly and you get smooth signal resolution throughout the day.

> thats not why i amaskiing, so filling 1000 share is basicly not even a cocnern
  ⎿  1 skill available

● Right — with 200-400M daily volume, filling 100 or even 1000 shares is nothing. Zero slippage concern. Market orders
  will fill instantly at the bid/ask with no impact on the price.

> has ther ebene any studies of teh relation of the daly vol and speed of excution / sliapege ?

● Web Search("academic study relationship daily trading volume execution speed slippage stock market microstructure")
  ⎿  Did 1 search in 7s

● Yes, this is well-studied in market microstructure research. The key finding:

  Square-root law of market impact: Price impact scales as roughly ~ sigma * sqrt(Q / V) where Q is your order size and
  V is daily volume. For SOFI doing 300M shares/day, a 1000-share order is Q/V = 0.000003 — essentially zero impact.

  Rule of thumb from the research: If your order is <1% of average daily volume (ADV), slippage is negligible. 1000
  shares on SOFI is 0.0003% of ADV. You'd need to be trading 300k+ shares to even start measuring slippage.

  Key papers:
  - Almgren & Chriss (2000) — optimal execution framework, shows impact is proportional to sqrt(order_size / volume)
  - The "square-root law" confirmed across markets — doubling volume halves the impact per share

  For your pipeline at 100-1000 shares on SOFI, execution is effectively instant at mid-price. The delayed execution
  columns (d_pnl) in scan.py measuring step+1 price difference will capture more slippage than the actual market impact.

  Sources:
  - https://mfe.baruch.cuny.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Chicago2016OptimalExecution.pdf
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1103.2214
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1302.4592
  - https://www.aeaweb.org/conference/2025/program/paper/ZsFFtySn
  - https://www.stocktitan.net/articles/bid-ask-spread-slippage-explained

  processes one step at a time.

      661
      662 +    def _lookup_step(self, step_num):
      663 +        """Look up close and reading for a given step from aggregate + signals.
      664 +        Returns (close, reading) or (None, None)."""
      665 +        if self._cached_df is None:
      666 +            return None, None
      667 +        df = self._cached_df
      668 +        if 'step' not in df.columns:
      669 +            return None, None
      670 +        mask = df['step'] == step_num
      671 +        if not mask.any():
      672 +            return None, None
      673 +        idx = mask.idxmax()
      674 +        close = float(self._cached_close_values[idx])
      675 +        # Find reading from signals list
      676 +        reading = None
      677 +        for sig in self.signals:
      678 +            if sig['step'] == step_num:
      679 +                reading = sig.get('signal')
      680 +                break
      681 +        return close, reading
      682 +
      683 +    def _fill_delayed_fields(self, trade):
      684 +        """Fill d_entry, d_exit, d_pnl from step+1 lookups."""
      685 +        # Delayed entry: step+1 after entry
      686 +        d_entry_step = trade["entry_step"] + 1
      687 +        d_entry_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_entry_step)
      688 +        trade["d_entry_step"] = d_entry_step
      689 +        trade["d_entry_close"] = d_entry_close
      690 +
      691 +        # Delayed exit: step+1 after exit
      692 +        if trade["exit_step"] is not None:
      693 +            d_exit_step = trade["exit_step"] + 1
      694 +            d_exit_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_exit_step)
      695 +            trade["d_exit_step"] = d_exit_step
      696 +            trade["d_exit_close"] = d_exit_close
      697 +
      698 +            if d_entry_close is not None and d_exit_close is not None:
      699 +                if trade["side"] == "call":
      700 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_exit_close - d_entry_close, 4)
      701 +                else:
      702 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_entry_close - d_exit_close, 4)
      703 +
      704 +    def _fill_sl_exit_fields(self, trade):
      705 +        """Fill sl*_next_step, sl*_next_close, sl*_next_reading, sl*_exit_pnl."""
      706 +        for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      707 +            sl_step = trade.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      708 +            if sl_step is not None:
      709 +                next_step = int(sl_step) + 1
      710 +                next_close, next_reading = self._lookup_step(next_step)
      711 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_step"] = next_step
      712 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_close"] = next_close
      713 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_reading"] = next_reading
      714 +                if next_close is not None:
      715 +                    if trade["side"] == "call":
      716 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(next_close - trade["entry_close"], 4)
      717 +                    else:
      718 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(trade["entry_close"] - next_close, 4)
      719 +
      720      def _close_trade(self, trade, step, close, wma, reason):
      663 -        """Close a trade, compute PNL, append to trades list."""
      721 +        """Close a trade, compute PNL, fill delayed/SL fields, append to trades list."""

      724          trade["max_pnl"] = round(trade["max_pnl"], 4)

● Header now shows: Trades - X total (Y closed: W=Z L=Z) | PNL: +X.XXXX | dPNL: +X.XXXX

> waht the import the module is using for iamge top bottom recodtion ?

● scan.py's detect_signal() uses:

  - OpenCV (cv2) — cv2.cvtColor for grayscale, cv2.Canny for edge detection
  - scipy (scipy.signal.find_peaks) — finds peaks (tops) and valleys (bottoms) in the smoothed edge curve
  - scipy (scipy.ndimage.gaussian_filter1d) — smooths the edge y-values before peak finding

  The flow:
  1. cv2.Canny(gray, 50, 150) — finds edges in the WMA line image
  2. For each x column, average the y-coordinates of edge pixels
  3. gaussian_filter1d(y_vals, sigma=1) — smooth the curve
  4. find_peaks(y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds bottoms (valleys)
  5. find_peaks(-y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds tops (peaks)
  6. Rightmost bottom > rightmost top → call, otherwise → put

✻ Sautéed for 34s

> sofi is hi vol stock ?

● Yes, SOFI (SoFi Technologies) is a high volume stock. It typically trades 200-400M+ shares daily, making it one of the
   most actively traded stocks on NASDAQ. That's why the 720k/1440k volume bar thresholds work — with that much volume,
  bars fill quickly and you get smooth signal resolution throughout the day.

> thats not why i amaskiing, so filling 1000 share is basicly not even a cocnern
  ⎿  1 skill available

● Right — with 200-400M daily volume, filling 100 or even 1000 shares is nothing. Zero slippage concern. Market orders
  will fill instantly at the bid/ask with no impact on the price.

> has ther ebene any studies of teh relation of the daly vol and speed of excution / sliapege ?

● Web Search("academic study relationship daily trading volume execution speed slippage stock market microstructure")
  ⎿  Did 1 search in 7s

● Yes, this is well-studied in market microstructure research. The key finding:

  Square-root law of market impact: Price impact scales as roughly ~ sigma * sqrt(Q / V) where Q is your order size and
  V is daily volume. For SOFI doing 300M shares/day, a 1000-share order is Q/V = 0.000003 — essentially zero impact.

  Rule of thumb from the research: If your order is <1% of average daily volume (ADV), slippage is negligible. 1000
  shares on SOFI is 0.0003% of ADV. You'd need to be trading 300k+ shares to even start measuring slippage.

  Key papers:
  - Almgren & Chriss (2000) — optimal execution framework, shows impact is proportional to sqrt(order_size / volume)
  - The "square-root law" confirmed across markets — doubling volume halves the impact per share

  For your pipeline at 100-1000 shares on SOFI, execution is effectively instant at mid-price. The delayed execution
  columns (d_pnl) in scan.py measuring step+1 price difference will capture more slippage than the actual market impact.

  Sources:
  - https://mfe.baruch.cuny.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Chicago2016OptimalExecution.pdf
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1103.2214
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1302.4592
  - https://www.aeaweb.org/conference/2025/program/paper/ZsFFtySn
  - https://www.stocktitan.net/articles/bid-ask-spread-slippage-explained

      627 +    def _update_trade_minmax(self, trade, close, step):
      628 +        """Update min/max PNL and SL level triggers on open trade."""
      629 +        if trade["side"] == "call":
      630 +            unrealized = close - trade["entry_close"]
      631 +        else:
      632 +            unrealized = trade["entry_close"] - close
      633 +        unrealized = round(unrealized, 4)
      634 +        if unrealized < trade["min_pnl"]:
      635 +            trade["min_pnl"] = unrealized
      636 +        if unrealized > trade["max_pnl"]:
      637 +            trade["max_pnl"] = unrealized

      640 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_step"] = step

      853 +    def _update_trade_table(self):
      854 +        """Refresh the trades treeview from self.trades + current open trade."""
      855 +        for item in self.trade_tree.get_children():
      856 +            self.trade_tree.delete(item)
      857 +
      858 +        def _fmt(v, decimals=4):
      859 +            if v is None:
      860 +                return ""
      861 +            return f"{v:.{decimals}f}" if isinstance(v, float) else str(v)
      862 +
      863 +        def _fmt_pnl(v):
      864 +            if v is None:
      865 +                return ""
      866 +            return f"{v:+.4f}"
      867 +
      868 +        # All closed trades + current open trade
      869 +        all_trades = list(self.trades)
      870 +        if self.current_trade is not None:
      871 +            # Show open trade with live unrealized PNL
      872 +            t = dict(self.current_trade)
      873 +            t["exit_reason"] = "open"

      661
      662 +    def _lookup_step(self, step_num):
      663 +        """Look up close and reading for a given step from aggregate + signals.
      664 +        Returns (close, reading) or (None, None)."""
      665 +        if self._cached_df is None:
      666 +            return None, None
      667 +        df = self._cached_df
      668 +        if 'step' not in df.columns:
      669 +            return None, None
      670 +        mask = df['step'] == step_num
      671 +        if not mask.any():
      672 +            return None, None
      673 +        idx = mask.idxmax()
      674 +        close = float(self._cached_close_values[idx])
      675 +        # Find reading from signals list
      676 +        reading = None
      677 +        for sig in self.signals:
      678 +            if sig['step'] == step_num:
      679 +                reading = sig.get('signal')
      680 +                break
      681 +        return close, reading
      682 +
      683 +    def _fill_delayed_fields(self, trade):
      684 +        """Fill d_entry, d_exit, d_pnl from step+1 lookups."""
      685 +        # Delayed entry: step+1 after entry
      686 +        d_entry_step = trade["entry_step"] + 1
      687 +        d_entry_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_entry_step)
      688 +        trade["d_entry_step"] = d_entry_step
      689 +        trade["d_entry_close"] = d_entry_close
      690 +
      691 +        # Delayed exit: step+1 after exit
      692 +        if trade["exit_step"] is not None:
      693 +            d_exit_step = trade["exit_step"] + 1
      694 +            d_exit_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_exit_step)
      695 +            trade["d_exit_step"] = d_exit_step
      696 +            trade["d_exit_close"] = d_exit_close
      697 +
      698 +            if d_entry_close is not None and d_exit_close is not None:
      699 +                if trade["side"] == "call":
      700 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_exit_close - d_entry_close, 4)
      701 +                else:
      702 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_entry_close - d_exit_close, 4)
      703 +
      704 +    def _fill_sl_exit_fields(self, trade):
      705 +        """Fill sl*_next_step, sl*_next_close, sl*_next_reading, sl*_exit_pnl."""
      706 +        for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      707 +            sl_step = trade.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      708 +            if sl_step is not None:
      709 +                next_step = int(sl_step) + 1
      710 +                next_close, next_reading = self._lookup_step(next_step)
      711 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_step"] = next_step
      712 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_close"] = next_close
      713 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_reading"] = next_reading
      714 +                if next_close is not None:
      715 +                    if trade["side"] == "call":
      716 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(next_close - trade["entry_close"], 4)
      717 +                    else:
      718 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(trade["entry_close"] - next_close, 4)
      719 +

● Header now shows: Trades - X total (Y closed: W=Z L=Z) | PNL: +X.XXXX | dPNL: +X.XXXX

> waht the import the module is using for iamge top bottom recodtion ?

● scan.py's detect_signal() uses:

  - OpenCV (cv2) — cv2.cvtColor for grayscale, cv2.Canny for edge detection
  - scipy (scipy.signal.find_peaks) — finds peaks (tops) and valleys (bottoms) in the smoothed edge curve
  - scipy (scipy.ndimage.gaussian_filter1d) — smooths the edge y-values before peak finding

  The flow:
  1. cv2.Canny(gray, 50, 150) — finds edges in the WMA line image
  2. For each x column, average the y-coordinates of edge pixels
  3. gaussian_filter1d(y_vals, sigma=1) — smooth the curve
  4. find_peaks(y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds bottoms (valleys)
  5. find_peaks(-y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds tops (peaks)
  6. Rightmost bottom > rightmost top → call, otherwise → put

✻ Sautéed for 34s

> sofi is hi vol stock ?

● Yes, SOFI (SoFi Technologies) is a high volume stock. It typically trades 200-400M+ shares daily, making it one of the
   most actively traded stocks on NASDAQ. That's why the 720k/1440k volume bar thresholds work — with that much volume,
  bars fill quickly and you get smooth signal resolution throughout the day.

> thats not why i amaskiing, so filling 1000 share is basicly not even a cocnern
  ⎿  1 skill available

● Right — with 200-400M daily volume, filling 100 or even 1000 shares is nothing. Zero slippage concern. Market orders
  will fill instantly at the bid/ask with no impact on the price.

> has ther ebene any studies of teh relation of the daly vol and speed of excution / sliapege ?

● Web Search("academic study relationship daily trading volume execution speed slippage stock market microstructure")
  ⎿  Did 1 search in 7s

● Yes, this is well-studied in market microstructure research. The key finding:

  Square-root law of market impact: Price impact scales as roughly ~ sigma * sqrt(Q / V) where Q is your order size and
  V is daily volume. For SOFI doing 300M shares/day, a 1000-share order is Q/V = 0.000003 — essentially zero impact.

  Rule of thumb from the research: If your order is <1% of average daily volume (ADV), slippage is negligible. 1000
  shares on SOFI is 0.0003% of ADV. You'd need to be trading 300k+ shares to even start measuring slippage.

  Key papers:
  - Almgren & Chriss (2000) — optimal execution framework, shows impact is proportional to sqrt(order_size / volume)
  - The "square-root law" confirmed across markets — doubling volume halves the impact per share

  For your pipeline at 100-1000 shares on SOFI, execution is effectively instant at mid-price. The delayed execution
  columns (d_pnl) in scan.py measuring step+1 price difference will capture more slippage than the actual market impact.

  Sources:
  - https://mfe.baruch.cuny.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Chicago2016OptimalExecution.pdf
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1103.2214
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1302.4592
  - https://www.aeaweb.org/conference/2025/program/paper/ZsFFtySn
  - https://www.stocktitan.net/articles/bid-ask-spread-slippage-explained

✻ Crunched for 39s

> hmm so we can ealy try 10,000 shares if needed

● Yeah, 10,000 shares on SOFI is still only 0.003% of ADV. Completely invisible to the market. The bid/ask spread
  (~$0.01 on SOFI) is your only real cost — the market impact from 10k shares is basically zero.

  At that size the commission matters more than the slippage.

      33 +# Market open = 9:30 AM US/Eastern
      34 +# Auto-detect DST: Summer (Mar-Nov) = 13:30 UTC, Winter (Nov-Mar) = 14:30 UTC
      35 +import zoneinfo
      36 +
      37 +def _market_open_utc(date_str):
      38 +    """Return (hour, minute) in UTC for 9:30 AM Eastern on the given date."""
      39 +    from datetime import datetime as _dt
      40 +    eastern = zoneinfo.ZoneInfo("America/New_York")
      41 +    d = _dt.strptime(date_str, '%Y-%m-%d')
      42 +    local_open = d.replace(hour=9, minute=30, second=0, tzinfo=eastern)
      43 +    utc_open = local_open.astimezone(zoneinfo.ZoneInfo("UTC"))
      44 +    return utc_open.hour, utc_open.minute
      45 +

      853 +    def _update_trade_table(self):
      854 +        """Refresh the trades treeview from self.trades + current open trade."""
      855 +        for item in self.trade_tree.get_children():
      856 +            self.trade_tree.delete(item)
      857 +
      858 +        def _fmt(v, decimals=4):
      859 +            if v is None:
      860 +                return ""
      861 +            return f"{v:.{decimals}f}" if isinstance(v, float) else str(v)
      862 +
      863 +        def _fmt_pnl(v):
      864 +            if v is None:
      865 +                return ""
      866 +            return f"{v:+.4f}"
      867 +
      868 +        # All closed trades + current open trade
      869 +        all_trades = list(self.trades)
      870 +        if self.current_trade is not None:
      871 +            # Show open trade with live unrealized PNL
      872 +            t = dict(self.current_trade)
      873 +            t["exit_reason"] = "open"
      874 +            if t["side"] == "call":
      875 +                t["pnl"] = round(self.current_close - t["entry_close"], 4)
      876 +            else:
      877 +                t["pnl"] = round(t["entry_close"] - self.current_close, 4)
      878 +            t["total_pnl"] = round(self.total_pnl + t["pnl"], 4)
      879 +            all_trades.append(t)
      880 +
      881 +        for t in all_trades:
      882 +            tag = 'open' if t.get("exit_reason") == "open" else ''
      883 +            if t.get("pnl") is not None and t["pnl"] > 0:
      884 +                tag = 'win' if t.get("exit_reason") != "open" else 'open'
      885 +            elif t.get("pnl") is not None and t["pnl"] < 0:
      886 +                tag = 'loss' if t.get("exit_reason") != "open" else 'open'
      887 +
      888 +            sl_vals = []
      889 +            for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      890 +                sl_step = t.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      891 +                sl_vals.append(str(int(sl_step)) if sl_step is not None else "")
      892 +
      893 +            self.trade_tree.insert('', 'end', values=(
      894 +                t["trade"], t["side"].upper(),
      895 +                t["entry_step"], _fmt(t["entry_close"]), _fmt(t["entry_wma55"]),
      896 +                t.get("exit_step") or "", _fmt(t.get("exit_close")), _fmt(t.get("exit_wma55")),
      897 +                t.get("exit_reason") or "",
      898 +                t["hold_steps"],
      899 +                _fmt_pnl(t["min_pnl"]), _fmt_pnl(t["max_pnl"]),
      900 +                _fmt_pnl(t.get("pnl")), _fmt_pnl(t.get("total_pnl")),
      901 +                *sl_vals,
      902 +            ), tags=(tag,))
      903 +
      904 +        self.trade_tree.tag_configure('win', foreground='#008800')
      905 +        self.trade_tree.tag_configure('loss', foreground='#CC0000')
      906 +        self.trade_tree.tag_configure('open', foreground='#0066CC')
      907 +
      908 +        # Auto-scroll
      909 +        children = self.trade_tree.get_children()
      910 +        if children:
      911 +            self.trade_tree.see(children[-1])
      912 +

      914 +        closed = [t for t in self.trades if t.get("exit_reason") != "open"]
      915 +        w = sum(1 for t in closed if t.get("pnl", 0) > 0)

      917 +        self.trade_header_label.config(

● Those delayed execution columns (d_*) and SL exit columns (sl*_next_*, sl*_exit_pnl) are only computed in scan.py's
  batch run_trades() — they need the full dataset to look up step+1 prices. The live GUI doesn't have them because it
  processes one step at a time.

  But we can compute them incrementally — we have all the step data in the aggregate. Let me add them.

      659              if trade[f"sl{sl}_step"] is None and unrealized <= -sl:

      662 +    def _lookup_step(self, step_num):
      663 +        """Look up close and reading for a given step from aggregate + signals.
      664 +        Returns (close, reading) or (None, None)."""
      665 +        if self._cached_df is None:
      666 +            return None, None
      667 +        df = self._cached_df
      668 +        if 'step' not in df.columns:
      669 +            return None, None
      670 +        mask = df['step'] == step_num
      671 +        if not mask.any():
      672 +            return None, None
      673 +        idx = mask.idxmax()
      674 +        close = float(self._cached_close_values[idx])
      675 +        # Find reading from signals list
      676 +        reading = None
      677 +        for sig in self.signals:
      678 +            if sig['step'] == step_num:
      679 +                reading = sig.get('signal')
      680 +                break
      681 +        return close, reading
      682 +
      683 +    def _fill_delayed_fields(self, trade):
      684 +        """Fill d_entry, d_exit, d_pnl from step+1 lookups."""
      685 +        # Delayed entry: step+1 after entry
      686 +        d_entry_step = trade["entry_step"] + 1
      687 +        d_entry_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_entry_step)
      688 +        trade["d_entry_step"] = d_entry_step
      689 +        trade["d_entry_close"] = d_entry_close
      690 +
      691 +        # Delayed exit: step+1 after exit
      692 +        if trade["exit_step"] is not None:
      693 +            d_exit_step = trade["exit_step"] + 1
      694 +            d_exit_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_exit_step)
      695 +            trade["d_exit_step"] = d_exit_step
      696 +            trade["d_exit_close"] = d_exit_close
      697 +
      698 +            if d_entry_close is not None and d_exit_close is not None:
      699 +                if trade["side"] == "call":
      700 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_exit_close - d_entry_close, 4)
      701 +                else:
      702 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_entry_close - d_exit_close, 4)
      703 +
      704 +    def _fill_sl_exit_fields(self, trade):
      705 +        """Fill sl*_next_step, sl*_next_close, sl*_next_reading, sl*_exit_pnl."""
      706 +        for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      707 +            sl_step = trade.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      708 +            if sl_step is not None:
      709 +                next_step = int(sl_step) + 1
      710 +                next_close, next_reading = self._lookup_step(next_step)
      711 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_step"] = next_step
      712 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_close"] = next_close
      713 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_reading"] = next_reading
      714 +                if next_close is not None:
      715 +                    if trade["side"] == "call":
      716 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(next_close - trade["entry_close"], 4)
      717 +                    else:
      718 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(trade["entry_close"] - next_close, 4)
      719 +
      720      def _close_trade(self, trade, step, close, wma, reason):
      663 -        """Close a trade, compute PNL, append to trades list."""
      721 +        """Close a trade, compute PNL, fill delayed/SL fields, append to trades list."""
      722          self._update_trade_minmax(trade, close, step)
      723          trade["min_pnl"] = round(trade["min_pnl"], 4)
      724          trade["max_pnl"] = round(trade["max_pnl"], 4)
     ...

      733          self.total_pnl += trade["pnl"]

      735 +        # Fill delayed and SL exit columns

● Header now shows: Trades - X total (Y closed: W=Z L=Z) | PNL: +X.XXXX | dPNL: +X.XXXX

> waht the import the module is using for iamge top bottom recodtion ?

● scan.py's detect_signal() uses:

  - OpenCV (cv2) — cv2.cvtColor for grayscale, cv2.Canny for edge detection
  - scipy (scipy.signal.find_peaks) — finds peaks (tops) and valleys (bottoms) in the smoothed edge curve
  - scipy (scipy.ndimage.gaussian_filter1d) — smooths the edge y-values before peak finding

  The flow:
  1. cv2.Canny(gray, 50, 150) — finds edges in the WMA line image
  2. For each x column, average the y-coordinates of edge pixels
  3. gaussian_filter1d(y_vals, sigma=1) — smooth the curve
  4. find_peaks(y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds bottoms (valleys)
  5. find_peaks(-y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds tops (peaks)
  6. Rightmost bottom > rightmost top → call, otherwise → put

> sofi is hi vol stock ?

● Yes, SOFI (SoFi Technologies) is a high volume stock. It typically trades 200-400M+ shares daily, making it one of the
   most actively traded stocks on NASDAQ. That's why the 720k/1440k volume bar thresholds work — with that much volume,
  bars fill quickly and you get smooth signal resolution throughout the day.

> thats not why i amaskiing, so filling 1000 share is basicly not even a cocnern
  ⎿  1 skill available

● Right — with 200-400M daily volume, filling 100 or even 1000 shares is nothing. Zero slippage concern. Market orders
  will fill instantly at the bid/ask with no impact on the price.

> has ther ebene any studies of teh relation of the daly vol and speed of excution / sliapege ?

● Web Search("academic study relationship daily trading volume execution speed slippage stock market microstructure")
  ⎿  Did 1 search in 7s

● Yes, this is well-studied in market microstructure research. The key finding:

  Square-root law of market impact: Price impact scales as roughly ~ sigma * sqrt(Q / V) where Q is your order size and
  V is daily volume. For SOFI doing 300M shares/day, a 1000-share order is Q/V = 0.000003 — essentially zero impact.

  Rule of thumb from the research: If your order is <1% of average daily volume (ADV), slippage is negligible. 1000
  shares on SOFI is 0.0003% of ADV. You'd need to be trading 300k+ shares to even start measuring slippage.

  Key papers:
  - Almgren & Chriss (2000) — optimal execution framework, shows impact is proportional to sqrt(order_size / volume)
  - The "square-root law" confirmed across markets — doubling volume halves the impact per share

  For your pipeline at 100-1000 shares on SOFI, execution is effectively instant at mid-price. The delayed execution
  columns (d_pnl) in scan.py measuring step+1 price difference will capture more slippage than the actual market impact.

  Sources:
  - https://mfe.baruch.cuny.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Chicago2016OptimalExecution.pdf
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1103.2214
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1302.4592
  - https://www.aeaweb.org/conference/2025/program/paper/ZsFFtySn
  - https://www.stocktitan.net/articles/bid-ask-spread-slippage-explained

✻ Crunched for 39s

> hmm so we can ealy try 10,000 shares if needed

● Yeah, 10,000 shares on SOFI is still only 0.003% of ADV. Completely invisible to the market. The bid/ask spread
  (~$0.01 on SOFI) is your only real cost — the market impact from 10k shares is basically zero.

  At that size the commission matters more than the slippage.

      627 +    def _update_trade_minmax(self, trade, close, step):
      628 +        """Update min/max PNL and SL level triggers on open trade."""

      853 +    def _update_trade_table(self):
      854 +        """Refresh the trades treeview from self.trades + current open trade."""
      855 +        for item in self.trade_tree.get_children():
      856 +            self.trade_tree.delete(item)
      857 +
      858 +        def _fmt(v, decimals=4):
      859 +            if v is None:
      860 +                return ""
      861 +            return f"{v:.{decimals}f}" if isinstance(v, float) else str(v)
      862 +
      863 +        def _fmt_pnl(v):
      864 +            if v is None:
      865 +                return ""
      866 +            return f"{v:+.4f}"
      867 +
      868 +        # All closed trades + current open trade
      869 +        all_trades = list(self.trades)

      871 +            # Show open trade with live unrealized PNL
      872 +            t = dict(self.current_trade)
      873 +            t["exit_reason"] = "open"
      874 +            if t["side"] == "call":
      875 +                t["pnl"] = round(self.current_close - t["entry_close"], 4)
      876 +            else:
      877 +                t["pnl"] = round(t["entry_close"] - self.current_close, 4)
      878 +            t["total_pnl"] = round(self.total_pnl + t["pnl"], 4)
      879 +            all_trades.append(t)
      880 +
      881 +        for t in all_trades:
      882 +            tag = 'open' if t.get("exit_reason") == "open" else ''
      883 +            if t.get("pnl") is not None and t["pnl"] > 0:
      884 +                tag = 'win' if t.get("exit_reason") != "open" else 'open'
      885 +            elif t.get("pnl") is not None and t["pnl"] < 0:
      886 +                tag = 'loss' if t.get("exit_reason") != "open" else 'open'
      887 +

      890 +                sl_step = t.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      891 +                sl_vals.append(str(int(sl_step)) if sl_step is not None else "")
      892 +
      893 +            self.trade_tree.insert('', 'end', values=(
      894 +                t["trade"], t["side"].upper(),
      895 +                t["entry_step"], _fmt(t["entry_close"]), _fmt(t["entry_wma55"]),
      896 +                t.get("exit_step") or "", _fmt(t.get("exit_close")), _fmt(t.get("exit_wma55")),
      897 +                t.get("exit_reason") or "",

      901 +                *sl_vals,

      662 +    def _lookup_step(self, step_num):
      663 +        """Look up close and reading for a given step from aggregate + signals.
      664 +        Returns (close, reading) or (None, None)."""
      665 +        if self._cached_df is None:
      666 +            return None, None
      667 +        df = self._cached_df
      668 +        if 'step' not in df.columns:
      669 +            return None, None
      670 +        mask = df['step'] == step_num
      671 +        if not mask.any():
      672 +            return None, None
      673 +        idx = mask.idxmax()
      674 +        close = float(self._cached_close_values[idx])
      675 +        # Find reading from signals list
      676 +        reading = None
      677 +        for sig in self.signals:
      678 +            if sig['step'] == step_num:
      679 +                reading = sig.get('signal')
      680 +                break
      681 +        return close, reading
      682 +
      683 +    def _fill_delayed_fields(self, trade):
      684 +        """Fill d_entry, d_exit, d_pnl from step+1 lookups."""
      685 +        # Delayed entry: step+1 after entry
      686 +        d_entry_step = trade["entry_step"] + 1
      687 +        d_entry_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_entry_step)
      688 +        trade["d_entry_step"] = d_entry_step
      689 +        trade["d_entry_close"] = d_entry_close
      690 +
      691 +        # Delayed exit: step+1 after exit
      692 +        if trade["exit_step"] is not None:
      693 +            d_exit_step = trade["exit_step"] + 1
      694 +            d_exit_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_exit_step)
      695 +            trade["d_exit_step"] = d_exit_step
      696 +            trade["d_exit_close"] = d_exit_close
      697 +
      698 +            if d_entry_close is not None and d_exit_close is not None:
      699 +                if trade["side"] == "call":
      700 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_exit_close - d_entry_close, 4)
      701 +                else:
      702 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_entry_close - d_exit_close, 4)
      703 +
      704 +    def _fill_sl_exit_fields(self, trade):
      705 +        """Fill sl*_next_step, sl*_next_close, sl*_next_reading, sl*_exit_pnl."""
      706 +        for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      707 +            sl_step = trade.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      708 +            if sl_step is not None:
      709 +                next_step = int(sl_step) + 1
      710 +                next_close, next_reading = self._lookup_step(next_step)
      711 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_step"] = next_step
      712 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_close"] = next_close
      713 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_reading"] = next_reading
      714 +                if next_close is not None:
      715 +                    if trade["side"] == "call":
      716 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(next_close - trade["entry_close"], 4)
      717 +                    else:
      718 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(trade["entry_close"] - next_close, 4)

● Header now shows: Trades - X total (Y closed: W=Z L=Z) | PNL: +X.XXXX | dPNL: +X.XXXX

> waht the import the module is using for iamge top bottom recodtion ?

● scan.py's detect_signal() uses:

  - OpenCV (cv2) — cv2.cvtColor for grayscale, cv2.Canny for edge detection
  - scipy (scipy.signal.find_peaks) — finds peaks (tops) and valleys (bottoms) in the smoothed edge curve
  - scipy (scipy.ndimage.gaussian_filter1d) — smooths the edge y-values before peak finding

  The flow:
  1. cv2.Canny(gray, 50, 150) — finds edges in the WMA line image
  2. For each x column, average the y-coordinates of edge pixels
  3. gaussian_filter1d(y_vals, sigma=1) — smooth the curve
  4. find_peaks(y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds bottoms (valleys)
  5. find_peaks(-y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds tops (peaks)
  6. Rightmost bottom > rightmost top → call, otherwise → put

> can we save those localy for version preservation ?

      print(f'scipy=={scipy.__version__}')" && python -c "import matplo…)
  ⎿  opencv-python==4.13.0
     scipy==1.17.1

✻ Sautéed for 34s

> sofi is hi vol stock ?

● Yes, SOFI (SoFi Technologies) is a high volume stock. It typically trades 200-400M+ shares daily, making it one of the
   most actively traded stocks on NASDAQ. That's why the 720k/1440k volume bar thresholds work — with that much volume,
  bars fill quickly and you get smooth signal resolution throughout the day.

> thats not why i amaskiing, so filling 1000 share is basicly not even a cocnern
  ⎿  1 skill available

● Right — with 200-400M daily volume, filling 100 or even 1000 shares is nothing. Zero slippage concern. Market orders
  will fill instantly at the bid/ask with no impact on the price.

> has ther ebene any studies of teh relation of the daly vol and speed of excution / sliapege ?

● Web Search("academic study relationship daily trading volume execution speed slippage stock market microstructure")
  ⎿  Did 1 search in 7s

● Yes, this is well-studied in market microstructure research. The key finding:

  Square-root law of market impact: Price impact scales as roughly ~ sigma * sqrt(Q / V) where Q is your order size and
  V is daily volume. For SOFI doing 300M shares/day, a 1000-share order is Q/V = 0.000003 — essentially zero impact.

  Rule of thumb from the research: If your order is <1% of average daily volume (ADV), slippage is negligible. 1000
  shares on SOFI is 0.0003% of ADV. You'd need to be trading 300k+ shares to even start measuring slippage.

  Key papers:
  - Almgren & Chriss (2000) — optimal execution framework, shows impact is proportional to sqrt(order_size / volume)
  - The "square-root law" confirmed across markets — doubling volume halves the impact per share

  For your pipeline at 100-1000 shares on SOFI, execution is effectively instant at mid-price. The delayed execution
  columns (d_pnl) in scan.py measuring step+1 price difference will capture more slippage than the actual market impact.

  Sources:
  - https://mfe.baruch.cuny.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Chicago2016OptimalExecution.pdf
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1103.2214
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1302.4592
  - https://www.aeaweb.org/conference/2025/program/paper/ZsFFtySn
  - https://www.stocktitan.net/articles/bid-ask-spread-slippage-explained

✻ Crunched for 39s

> hmm so we can ealy try 10,000 shares if needed

● Yeah, 10,000 shares on SOFI is still only 0.003% of ADV. Completely invisible to the market. The bid/ask spread
  (~$0.01 on SOFI) is your only real cost — the market impact from 10k shares is basically zero.

  At that size the commission matters more than the slippage.

> hwo deo sit open logn and short trade, as acoding to ib documted aproach ?

● Looking at the current execute_stock() in ib_broker.py:

  # CALL side: Buy→BUY shares, Sell→SELL shares
  # PUT side:  Buy→SELL shares (short), Sell→BUY shares (cover)

  So when the pipeline signals a call (go long):
  - execute_stock('Buy', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'CALL') → sends BUY 100 to IB

  When it flips to put (go short), two orders:
  1. execute_stock('Sell', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'CALL') → sends SELL 100 (closes long)
  2. execute_stock('Buy', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'PUT') → sends SELL 100 (opens short)

  That's two separate SELL 100 orders hitting IB back-to-back.

  IB handles this natively — it doesn't care about your "position" at the order level. First SELL 100 closes the long,
  second SELL 100 opens a short. The account just goes from +100 to 0 to -100.

  For shorting specifically, IB requires:
  - The stock must be locatable (shortable) — SOFI is heavily traded so always available
  - Margin account (not cash)
  - IB auto-locates the borrow, no extra API call needed
  - Short sales follow reg SHO — IB handles the uptick rule compliance

  The MarketOrder('SELL', qty) is the same whether closing a long or opening a short. IB figures it out from your
  current position.

      613 +    def _open_trade(self, side, step, close, wma):
      614 +        """Create a new trade dict matching scan.py format."""
      615 +        t = {
      616 +            "trade": self.trade_num, "side": side,
      617 +            "entry_step": step, "entry_close": close, "entry_wma55": wma,
      618 +            "exit_step": None, "exit_close": None, "exit_wma55": None,
      619 +            "exit_reason": None, "hold_steps": 0,

      622 +        }

      624 +            t[f"sl{sl}_step"] = None

      626 +
      627 +    def _update_trade_minmax(self, trade, close, step):
      628 +        """Update min/max PNL and SL level triggers on open trade."""
      629 +        if trade["side"] == "call":
      630 +            unrealized = close - trade["entry_close"]
      631 +        else:
      632 +            unrealized = trade["entry_close"] - close
      633 +        unrealized = round(unrealized, 4)
      634 +        if unrealized < trade["min_pnl"]:
      635 +            trade["min_pnl"] = unrealized
      636 +        if unrealized > trade["max_pnl"]:
      637 +            trade["max_pnl"] = unrealized
      638 +        for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      639 +            if trade[f"sl{sl}_step"] is None and unrealized <= -sl:
      640 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_step"] = step

      659              if trade[f"sl{sl}_step"] is None and unrealized <= -sl:

      661
      662 +    def _lookup_step(self, step_num):
      663 +        """Look up close and reading for a given step from aggregate + signals.
      664 +        Returns (close, reading) or (None, None)."""
      665 +        if self._cached_df is None:
      666 +            return None, None
      667 +        df = self._cached_df
      668 +        if 'step' not in df.columns:
      669 +            return None, None
      670 +        mask = df['step'] == step_num
      671 +        if not mask.any():
      672 +            return None, None
      673 +        idx = mask.idxmax()
      674 +        close = float(self._cached_close_values[idx])
      675 +        # Find reading from signals list
      676 +        reading = None
      677 +        for sig in self.signals:
      678 +            if sig['step'] == step_num:
      679 +                reading = sig.get('signal')
      680 +                break
      681 +        return close, reading
      682 +
      683 +    def _fill_delayed_fields(self, trade):
      684 +        """Fill d_entry, d_exit, d_pnl from step+1 lookups."""
      685 +        # Delayed entry: step+1 after entry
      686 +        d_entry_step = trade["entry_step"] + 1
      687 +        d_entry_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_entry_step)
      688 +        trade["d_entry_step"] = d_entry_step
      689 +        trade["d_entry_close"] = d_entry_close
      690 +
      691 +        # Delayed exit: step+1 after exit
      692 +        if trade["exit_step"] is not None:
      693 +            d_exit_step = trade["exit_step"] + 1
      694 +            d_exit_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_exit_step)
      695 +            trade["d_exit_step"] = d_exit_step
      696 +            trade["d_exit_close"] = d_exit_close
      697 +
      698 +            if d_entry_close is not None and d_exit_close is not None:
      699 +                if trade["side"] == "call":
      700 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_exit_close - d_entry_close, 4)
      701 +                else:
      702 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_entry_close - d_exit_close, 4)
      703 +
      704 +    def _fill_sl_exit_fields(self, trade):
      705 +        """Fill sl*_next_step, sl*_next_close, sl*_next_reading, sl*_exit_pnl."""
      706 +        for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      707 +            sl_step = trade.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      708 +            if sl_step is not None:
      709 +                next_step = int(sl_step) + 1
      710 +                next_close, next_reading = self._lookup_step(next_step)
      711 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_step"] = next_step
      712 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_close"] = next_close
      713 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_reading"] = next_reading
      714 +                if next_close is not None:
      715 +                    if trade["side"] == "call":
      716 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(next_close - trade["entry_close"], 4)
      717 +                    else:
      718 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(trade["entry_close"] - next_close, 4)
      719 +
      720      def _close_trade(self, trade, step, close, wma, reason):
      663 -        """Close a trade, compute PNL, append to trades list."""
      721 +        """Close a trade, compute PNL, fill delayed/SL fields, append to trades list."""
      722          self._update_trade_minmax(trade, close, step)
      723          trade["min_pnl"] = round(trade["min_pnl"], 4)
      724          trade["max_pnl"] = round(trade["max_pnl"], 4)
     ...

● Header now shows: Trades - X total (Y closed: W=Z L=Z) | PNL: +X.XXXX | dPNL: +X.XXXX

> waht the import the module is using for iamge top bottom recodtion ?

● scan.py's detect_signal() uses:

  - OpenCV (cv2) — cv2.cvtColor for grayscale, cv2.Canny for edge detection
  - scipy (scipy.signal.find_peaks) — finds peaks (tops) and valleys (bottoms) in the smoothed edge curve
  - scipy (scipy.ndimage.gaussian_filter1d) — smooths the edge y-values before peak finding

  The flow:
  1. cv2.Canny(gray, 50, 150) — finds edges in the WMA line image
  2. For each x column, average the y-coordinates of edge pixels
  3. gaussian_filter1d(y_vals, sigma=1) — smooth the curve
  4. find_peaks(y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds bottoms (valleys)
  5. find_peaks(-y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds tops (peaks)
  6. Rightmost bottom > rightmost top → call, otherwise → put

✻ Sautéed for 34s

> sofi is hi vol stock ?

● Yes, SOFI (SoFi Technologies) is a high volume stock. It typically trades 200-400M+ shares daily, making it one of the
   most actively traded stocks on NASDAQ. That's why the 720k/1440k volume bar thresholds work — with that much volume,
  bars fill quickly and you get smooth signal resolution throughout the day.

> thats not why i amaskiing, so filling 1000 share is basicly not even a cocnern
  ⎿  1 skill available

● Right — with 200-400M daily volume, filling 100 or even 1000 shares is nothing. Zero slippage concern. Market orders
  will fill instantly at the bid/ask with no impact on the price.

> has ther ebene any studies of teh relation of the daly vol and speed of excution / sliapege ?

● Web Search("academic study relationship daily trading volume execution speed slippage stock market microstructure")
  ⎿  Did 1 search in 7s

● Yes, this is well-studied in market microstructure research. The key finding:

  Square-root law of market impact: Price impact scales as roughly ~ sigma * sqrt(Q / V) where Q is your order size and
  V is daily volume. For SOFI doing 300M shares/day, a 1000-share order is Q/V = 0.000003 — essentially zero impact.

  Rule of thumb from the research: If your order is <1% of average daily volume (ADV), slippage is negligible. 1000
  shares on SOFI is 0.0003% of ADV. You'd need to be trading 300k+ shares to even start measuring slippage.

  Key papers:
  - Almgren & Chriss (2000) — optimal execution framework, shows impact is proportional to sqrt(order_size / volume)
  - The "square-root law" confirmed across markets — doubling volume halves the impact per share

  For your pipeline at 100-1000 shares on SOFI, execution is effectively instant at mid-price. The delayed execution
  columns (d_pnl) in scan.py measuring step+1 price difference will capture more slippage than the actual market impact.

  Sources:
  - https://mfe.baruch.cuny.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Chicago2016OptimalExecution.pdf
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1103.2214
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1302.4592
  - https://www.aeaweb.org/conference/2025/program/paper/ZsFFtySn
  - https://www.stocktitan.net/articles/bid-ask-spread-slippage-explained

✻ Crunched for 39s

> hmm so we can ealy try 10,000 shares if needed

● Yeah, 10,000 shares on SOFI is still only 0.003% of ADV. Completely invisible to the market. The bid/ask spread
  (~$0.01 on SOFI) is your only real cost — the market impact from 10k shares is basically zero.

  At that size the commission matters more than the slippage.

> hwo deo sit open logn and short trade, as acoding to ib documted aproach ?

● Looking at the current execute_stock() in ib_broker.py:

  # CALL side: Buy→BUY shares, Sell→SELL shares
  # PUT side:  Buy→SELL shares (short), Sell→BUY shares (cover)

  So when the pipeline signals a call (go long):
  - execute_stock('Buy', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'CALL') → sends BUY 100 to IB

  When it flips to put (go short), two orders:
  1. execute_stock('Sell', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'CALL') → sends SELL 100 (closes long)
  2. execute_stock('Buy', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'PUT') → sends SELL 100 (opens short)

  That's two separate SELL 100 orders hitting IB back-to-back.

  IB handles this natively — it doesn't care about your "position" at the order level. First SELL 100 closes the long,
  second SELL 100 opens a short. The account just goes from +100 to 0 to -100.

  For shorting specifically, IB requires:
  - The stock must be locatable (shortable) — SOFI is heavily traded so always available
  - Margin account (not cash)
  - IB auto-locates the borrow, no extra API call needed
  - Short sales follow reg SHO — IB handles the uptick rule compliance

  The MarketOrder('SELL', qty) is the same whether closing a long or opening a short. IB figures it out from your
  current position.

      661
      662 +    def _lookup_step(self, step_num):
      663 +        """Look up close and reading for a given step from aggregate + signals.
      664 +        Returns (close, reading) or (None, None)."""
      665 +        if self._cached_df is None:
      666 +            return None, None
      667 +        df = self._cached_df
      668 +        if 'step' not in df.columns:
      669 +            return None, None
      670 +        mask = df['step'] == step_num
      671 +        if not mask.any():
      672 +            return None, None
      673 +        idx = mask.idxmax()
      674 +        close = float(self._cached_close_values[idx])
      675 +        # Find reading from signals list
      676 +        reading = None
      677 +        for sig in self.signals:
      678 +            if sig['step'] == step_num:
      679 +                reading = sig.get('signal')
      680 +                break
      681 +        return close, reading
      682 +
      683 +    def _fill_delayed_fields(self, trade):
      684 +        """Fill d_entry, d_exit, d_pnl from step+1 lookups."""
      685 +        # Delayed entry: step+1 after entry
      686 +        d_entry_step = trade["entry_step"] + 1
      687 +        d_entry_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_entry_step)
      688 +        trade["d_entry_step"] = d_entry_step
      689 +        trade["d_entry_close"] = d_entry_close
      690 +
      691 +        # Delayed exit: step+1 after exit
      692 +        if trade["exit_step"] is not None:
      693 +            d_exit_step = trade["exit_step"] + 1
      694 +            d_exit_close, _ = self._lookup_step(d_exit_step)
      695 +            trade["d_exit_step"] = d_exit_step
      696 +            trade["d_exit_close"] = d_exit_close
      697 +
      698 +            if d_entry_close is not None and d_exit_close is not None:
      699 +                if trade["side"] == "call":
      700 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_exit_close - d_entry_close, 4)
      701 +                else:
      702 +                    trade["d_pnl"] = round(d_entry_close - d_exit_close, 4)
      703 +
      704 +    def _fill_sl_exit_fields(self, trade):
      705 +        """Fill sl*_next_step, sl*_next_close, sl*_next_reading, sl*_exit_pnl."""
      706 +        for sl in scan.SL_LEVELS:
      707 +            sl_step = trade.get(f"sl{sl}_step")
      708 +            if sl_step is not None:
      709 +                next_step = int(sl_step) + 1
      710 +                next_close, next_reading = self._lookup_step(next_step)
      711 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_step"] = next_step
      712 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_close"] = next_close
      713 +                trade[f"sl{sl}_next_reading"] = next_reading
      714 +                if next_close is not None:
      715 +                    if trade["side"] == "call":
      716 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(next_close - trade["entry_close"], 4)
      717 +                    else:
      718 +                        trade[f"sl{sl}_exit_pnl"] = round(trade["entry_close"] - next_close, 4)
      719 +
      720      def _close_trade(self, trade, step, close, wma, reason):

      721 +        """Close a trade, compute PNL, fill delayed/SL fields, append to trades list."""

● Header now shows: Trades - X total (Y closed: W=Z L=Z) | PNL: +X.XXXX | dPNL: +X.XXXX

> waht the import the module is using for iamge top bottom recodtion ?

● scan.py's detect_signal() uses:

  - OpenCV (cv2) — cv2.cvtColor for grayscale, cv2.Canny for edge detection
  - scipy (scipy.signal.find_peaks) — finds peaks (tops) and valleys (bottoms) in the smoothed edge curve
  - scipy (scipy.ndimage.gaussian_filter1d) — smooths the edge y-values before peak finding

  The flow:
  1. cv2.Canny(gray, 50, 150) — finds edges in the WMA line image
  2. For each x column, average the y-coordinates of edge pixels
  3. gaussian_filter1d(y_vals, sigma=1) — smooth the curve
  4. find_peaks(y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds bottoms (valleys)
  5. find_peaks(-y_smooth, distance=15, prominence=5) — finds tops (peaks)
  6. Rightmost bottom > rightmost top → call, otherwise → put

✻ Sautéed for 34s

> sofi is hi vol stock ?

● Yes, SOFI (SoFi Technologies) is a high volume stock. It typically trades 200-400M+ shares daily, making it one of the
   most actively traded stocks on NASDAQ. That's why the 720k/1440k volume bar thresholds work — with that much volume,
  bars fill quickly and you get smooth signal resolution throughout the day.

> thats not why i amaskiing, so filling 1000 share is basicly not even a cocnern
  ⎿  1 skill available

● Right — with 200-400M daily volume, filling 100 or even 1000 shares is nothing. Zero slippage concern. Market orders
  will fill instantly at the bid/ask with no impact on the price.

> has ther ebene any studies of teh relation of the daly vol and speed of excution / sliapege ?

● Web Search("academic study relationship daily trading volume execution speed slippage stock market microstructure")
  ⎿  Did 1 search in 7s

● Yes, this is well-studied in market microstructure research. The key finding:

  Square-root law of market impact: Price impact scales as roughly ~ sigma * sqrt(Q / V) where Q is your order size and
  V is daily volume. For SOFI doing 300M shares/day, a 1000-share order is Q/V = 0.000003 — essentially zero impact.

  Rule of thumb from the research: If your order is <1% of average daily volume (ADV), slippage is negligible. 1000
  shares on SOFI is 0.0003% of ADV. You'd need to be trading 300k+ shares to even start measuring slippage.

  Key papers:
  - Almgren & Chriss (2000) — optimal execution framework, shows impact is proportional to sqrt(order_size / volume)
  - The "square-root law" confirmed across markets — doubling volume halves the impact per share

  For your pipeline at 100-1000 shares on SOFI, execution is effectively instant at mid-price. The delayed execution
  columns (d_pnl) in scan.py measuring step+1 price difference will capture more slippage than the actual market impact.

  Sources:
  - https://mfe.baruch.cuny.edu/wp-content/uploads/2012/09/Chicago2016OptimalExecution.pdf
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1103.2214
  - https://arxiv.org/pdf/1302.4592
  - https://www.aeaweb.org/conference/2025/program/paper/ZsFFtySn
  - https://www.stocktitan.net/articles/bid-ask-spread-slippage-explained

✻ Crunched for 39s

> hmm so we can ealy try 10,000 shares if needed

● Yeah, 10,000 shares on SOFI is still only 0.003% of ADV. Completely invisible to the market. The bid/ask spread
  (~$0.01 on SOFI) is your only real cost — the market impact from 10k shares is basically zero.

  At that size the commission matters more than the slippage.

> hwo deo sit open logn and short trade, as acoding to ib documted aproach ?

● Looking at the current execute_stock() in ib_broker.py:

  # CALL side: Buy→BUY shares, Sell→SELL shares
  # PUT side:  Buy→SELL shares (short), Sell→BUY shares (cover)

  So when the pipeline signals a call (go long):
  - execute_stock('Buy', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'CALL') → sends BUY 100 to IB

  When it flips to put (go short), two orders:
  1. execute_stock('Sell', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'CALL') → sends SELL 100 (closes long)
  2. execute_stock('Buy', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'PUT') → sends SELL 100 (opens short)

  That's two separate SELL 100 orders hitting IB back-to-back.

  IB handles this natively — it doesn't care about your "position" at the order level. First SELL 100 closes the long,
  second SELL 100 opens a short. The account just goes from +100 to 0 to -100.

  For shorting specifically, IB requires:
  - The stock must be locatable (shortable) — SOFI is heavily traded so always available
  - Margin account (not cash)
  - IB auto-locates the borrow, no extra API call needed
  - Short sales follow reg SHO — IB handles the uptick rule compliance

  The MarketOrder('SELL', qty) is the same whether closing a long or opening a short. IB figures it out from your
  current position.

> and whenit flip form put to call regime and we are doing stock mdoe it buys 100 to close tu eh short and then seon
trade it buys 100 new posiiton

● Exactly. Put→call flip sends:

  1. execute_stock('Sell', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'PUT') → maps to BUY 100 (covers the short)
  2. execute_stock('Buy', 'SOFI', 100, step, 'CALL') → maps to BUY 100 (opens long)

  Two separate BUY 100 orders. Account goes from -100 → 0 → +100.
